a prayer for the brick cathedral facing st paul 's : bankside power station is a masterpiece worth , preserving , gavin stamp argues
by gavin stamp
from the top of the dome of st paul 's cathedral the view is no longer dominated by city church steeple but by an intrusive cacophony of drab , characterless sixty box .
one building stand out in this dispiriting panorama of post-war mediocrity : a dark powerful mass of brickwork with a tall central tower that stand right across the thames from wren 's dome .
this is not an office block , nor a church â€” although it sublime form might suggest that it architect wa adept at designing cathedral .
it is , in fact , the now redundant oil-fired electric power station that sits on bankside next to the site of sam wanamaker 's new globe theatre .
bankside power station should never have been built .
it architect had spent the war year with fellow royal academician planning the orderly and spacious london of the future , free of smoke and industry .
but , when asked in 1947 to replace an old dirty power station that had been on the site since 1891 , he soon forgot such idealism and , like any architect , wa glad to have the job .
the project wa controversial and the power station wa only permitted providing the smoke wa clean and the building did not challenge the visual dominance of st paul 's .
so the single chimney rose only to 325ft , some 45ft below the height of the cross above the cathedral .
the irony is that had the tower been higher and had the teak â€˜ scrubber â€™ been le efficient , the smoke would have gone straight up into the air .
a it wa , the â€˜ smokeless shimmer of vapour â€™ wa so cooled by cleaning that it drifted across the river to cause mischief with the leadwork on wren 's great dome .
bankside power station should not have been built .
but , a it wa built , it should not now be demolished .
that is because it is a magnificent structure , the supreme architectural expression of the heroic , monumental phase of power station design and the creation of a great architect .
bankside wa the work of sir giles gilbert scott , om , the architect of liverpool 's anglican cathedral , the rebuilt house of common and some of the last vital product of the gothic revival .
he wa a designer of extraordinary versatility , being responsible for the standard â€˜ traditional â€™ red telephone kiosk , waterloo bridge and several power station .
bankside represents the fullest realisation of his industrial aesthetic .
scott 's first venture into this unlikely field of design wa at battersea where , in 1930 , he wa wheeled in a a famous knighted architect by the london power company to try to make acceptable the coal-fired monster power station to which the resident of chelsea and westminster were taking strong exception .
this wa a brilliant move .
scott wa so successful in styling the building in fine brickwork with â€˜ jazz-modern â€™ fluting ( a john betjeman called it ) that , when the battersea â€˜ a â€™ station wa opened in 1934 it wa widely acclaimed a a supremely successful modern treatment of a building type that seemed quintessentially twentieth century .
when , in 1939 , the architect ' journal conducted a survey to find what were considered the best modern building in britain , battersea wa placed second â€” and wa the favourite of such unlikely celebrity a sir kenneth clark , rebecca west and charles laughton .
scott wa so pleased with the style he had evolved at battersea , a treatment that humanised industrial form without denying their function , that he also used it on the guinness factory at park royal , west london .
at battersea , scott could not alter the basic design of the building and he much disliked the â€˜ upturned table â€™ appearance created by the four corner chimney .
at bankside , however , he wa able to persuade the engineer , mott , hay & anderson , to gather all the flue into a single â€˜ slender tower or campanile â€™ .
a a result , he wa able to create a symmetrical , monumental composition of great power .
a at all his power station , scott faced the building in a fine worcestershire brick that ha weathered to a lovely pinky-brown .
but there is nothing homely about the general effect .
vast overlapping plane of brickwork are modelled with careful set-back and subtle band of detail .
the result is an expression of the monumental aesthetic of the early twentieth century , with strong american overtone .
when the campanile is seen from a distance , it seems to belong to some strange expressionist church one ha not noticed before .
not for nothing were such power station described a â€˜ brick cathedral â€™ ; bankside is the finest manifestation of this tradition .
now it is redundant .
smoke shimmer no longer from the tall tower .
but bankside is nevertheless a sound structure which , like the best mill of the industrial revolution , is well worth preserving and is perfectly capable of adaptation for a new commercial use .
such re-use is , of course , much encouraged by a building being listed , something which , until recently , wa not possible with architecture of so recent a date .
two year ago , however , the department of the environment at last began the listing of post-war building in england that were more than 30 year old .
bracken house , the former home of the financial time , became the first candidate and english heritage then submitted some 70 recommendation to the department of the environment ; these included bankside .
this , however , wa too much for the government and , using the excuse that public opinion wa not yet ready to accept the protection of many unpopular modern building , lord caithness , the minister of state for the environment , arbitrarily whittled down english heritage 's list to 18 building - excluding bankside â€” although it represented a more traditional approach in the fifty to the now-unfashionable modern movement .
however , caithness himself stated that this first selection wa â€˜ in no way a definitive list â€¦
i have no doubt that others will be added .
the important thing is that the thirty year rule is in force and that we can respond to developing perception of our time . â€™
earlier this year , in my capacity a chairman of the thirty society , i asked caithness 's successor , virginia bottomley , to reconsider english heritage 's recommendation of bankside for listing .
my argument wa that , a michael heseltine had so boldly listed battersea power station in 1980 , it wa illogical not to protect a much finer and more complete industrial work by the same architect .
furthermore , the listing of battersea had ensured the building 's survival for conversion to a new use â€” in that case , a an entertainment centre which the prime minister herself had praised and inaugurated .
after two month ' silence , i wa informed that minister stood by their decision .
i wrote back asking the reason for this , pointing out that , if any large modern power station deserved to be listed , it wa bankside .
i have received no satisfactory reply .
of course , i know perfectly well why the department of the environment decline to list it .
listed building procedure might impede the full commercial realisation of the site when the electricity industry is privatised .
furthermore , british rail ha it eye on the bankside site for bringing up the spoil from the tunnel for channel traffic which it is , so absurdly , driving under the middle of london at astronomical cost .
listing , in theory , is an objective assessment of architectural or historical importance which doe not necessarily prevent demolition .
in the case of bankside power station , the ultimate â€˜ temple of power â€™ and a masterpiece of industrial architecture by a major twentieth-century british architect , our historic building system is being perverted for purely political reason .
â€˜ her dress hang here' : de-frocking the kahlo cult
oriana baddeley
the 1990s have witnessed a shift in the art establishment 's attitude towards art produced outside of it traditional parameter .
the work of previously marginalised artist ha become an area of rich speculation among art dealer priced out of the â€˜ modern master â€™ market .
almost every year ha witnessed the discovery of new artistic terrain â€” graffiti art , soviet art , australian art , the art of latin america .
the major auction house have moved with the time and have found new way of selling work which in both form and content would have proved an unstable investment a decade ago .
the current status of the work of the mexican painter frida kahlo is a dramatic example of this change .
once known primarily a the wife of diego rivera , her reputation outside of mexico now far supercedes his : since 1919 , sale room estimate of her work have risen from $40,000 to over $1 million , and in 1990 a work by kahlo broke all record at sotheby 's new york for a latin american artist .
the enormous rise in the economic value of her work ha developed in tandem with the increased critical and popular response to her particular blend of naive style and incisive content .
while the first wave of popular interest arose with the 1982 whitechapel exhibition instigated by laura mulvey and peter wollen , it wa the publication of hayden herrera 's biography of kahlo in 1983 which ha led to her current cult status .
since that date she ha been the subject of tv documentary , a feature film ( â€˜ frida â€™ by paul leduc ) , a stage play , numerous publication and the inspiration for designer clothing .
in may 1989 elle magazine ran a 16 page feature on frida kahlo a the â€˜ spirit of mexico â€™ ( fig. 1 ) , while in vogue ( feb. 1990 ) there wa a 10 page interpretation of â€˜ the romance of frida kahlo 's mexico â€™ ( fig. 2 ) .
almost a a logical outcome of this medium blitz , it emerged in the summer of 1990 that madonna , already a devotee of kahlo 's work , wa commissioning a screenplay based on kahlo 's life .
fig. 1 .
elle magazine , may 1989 , p. 18â€“19 .
a with most artist who have become mythical personality in the popular imagination , such attention ha focused primarily on the anecdotal and tragic detail of kahlo 's admittedly fascinating life .
the passionate obsession with her husband diego rivera , her flamboyant appearance , but most of all her physical and emotional pain have come to dominate response to her work .
while kahlo 's art helped her to deal with the vicissitude of her life , for most audience it is her life story which allows access to her art .
in this one can draw obvious parallel to the appeal of van gogh , a traditionally popular artist recently made fashionable by the medium attention generated during the centennial of his death .
the archetypal dropout/spiritualist became an appropriate icon for the sixty revival of 1990 'm_s long hot summer .
yet despite the iconic status of van gogh 's â€˜ tragic â€™ life , it is the appearance of his work by which he is ultimately signified , his thick impasto brush-stroke , his vibrant yellow , the urgency of his creative drive .
in the case of kahlo the popular image is of the artist herself , the characteristic brow , the elaborate hair , the mexican costume ( fig. 3 ) .
it is primarily her appearance , not the formal language of her art , that ha graced the page of elle and vogue magazine .
the elle feature transposed the â€˜ kahlo style â€™ to kahlo lookalikes in contemporary clothing balanced around segment of herrera 's biography of the artist .
in the later vogue piece only the style remained a the far more overtly sexual , kahloesque model lounged and pouted in their â€˜ mexican â€™ interior .
there is a poignant irony in the way clothing , which on one level served to hide kahlo 's broken body , fall or is lifted by the model to reveal a luxuriantly perfect physique ( fig. 4 ) .
the visual reference in the two magazine are a much from photo of the artist a from her work .
in both feature she is also seen to embody a wider set of assumption about mexico itself ; exotic , passionate , yet constantly struggling against pain and deceit .
while elle , vogue and subsequently the independent ( fig. 5 ) , stressed different facet of kahlo 's public persona , they all shared the emphasis on â€˜ her â€™ , a an encapsulisation of stereotypical image of mexico , rather than her work .
it is her body a the canvas , her appearance a art .
the art of self-expression becomes self-expression a art .

vogue , february 1990 , p. 130â€“1 .
fig. 3 .
elle magazine , may 1989 , p. 28 .
of course , the line between art and life is a particularly hard one to draw in kahlo 's case .
the majority of her work is self portraiture ; her aesthetic concern grew from her fascination with the falsity of appearance .
dressing up , role playing and masquerade form the conceptual basis of kahlo 's work .
in self-portrait with cropped hair ( 1944 ) ( fig. 6 ) , she paint herself wearing rivera 's suit , challenging traditional expectation of femininity and attempting to appropriate his authority ( while simultaneously ) threatening castration ) .
more disturbingly , in the mask ( 1945 ) ( fig. 7 ) , she throw doubt on too straightforward a reading of her self-portrait a revealing of her inner emotion .
where doe the mask fall : doe not the ritual repetition of those familiar feature â€˜ mask â€™ far more than it uncovers ?
there is , however , an inevitable logic to the appropriation of her meticulously constructed image , a process which the artist wa mocking a early a 1933 : â€˜ â€¦ some of the gringa woman are imitating me and trying to dress â€˜ a la mexicana â€™ , but the poor soul only look like cabbage and to tell you the naked truth they look absolutely impossible . '
the â€˜ impossibility â€™ stemmed from the failure of such follower to recognise the symbolic importance of kahlo 's choice of clothing , a failure also intrinsic to her recent magazine appearance .
the particularity of post-revolutionary mexico are frequently subsumed by the decorativeness of the ethnic , by the generalised attractiveness of the radical avant-garde .
for kahlo , however , choosing to don the costume of the tehuana , a for example in tree of hope ( 1946 ) ( fig. 8 ) , wa to embody a powerful icon of cultural identity .
mexican indian dress is extraordinarily diverse and by and large geographically specific , varying from region to region .
the tehuana dress is by no mean the most decorative variant or the closest to pre-hispanic form of clothing .
it is the mythology surrounding the woman wearer of the costume which directed kahlo 's choice .
the ostensibly matriarchal society of tehuantepec led to the adoption of the tehuana , in post-revolutionary mexico , a the image of the strong indian woman ; the undefeated counterpart to the despised â€˜ chingada â€™ , who , conversely is the female embodiment of mexico 's hybrid post-conquest culture .
in a culture where sexual metaphor are frequently used to convey racial and political conflict , the tehuana represents that aspect of mexico 's indigenous tradition unbowed by century of colonial and male rule .
kahlo 's adoption of tehuana dress , while being an attractive disguise of what she saw a a le than perfect body , asserted both a feminist and an anti-colonialist position .

in kahlo 's work there is a powerful mix of these discourse , yet her role a an archetypal woman painter ha come to dominate response to her work .
it is through her emergence a a cult painter of the feminist movement of the 1970s that her current reputation ha evolved .
her work almost perfectly illustrates debate a to the nature of traditional exclusion of a woman 's art .
the fascination with function of the body , the analogy between artistic and physical creative process , self-portraiture used to reveal the female body a the site of patriarchal aesthetic discourse ; all of these mirror the concern of many woman painter of the 1980s .

in their formal language , kahlo 's work are exemplary of certain feminist argument ; the adoption of the decorative , the intimate and non-fine art medium reveals the restrictive nature of traditional definition of â€˜ high art â€™ .
this â€˜ appropriateness â€™ of kahlo 's aesthetic to contemporary debate ha tended to remove her work from it historical context , to stress the collective and the cross-cultural .
although this is not in itself to be dismissed a a tactic , it ha diminished the complexity of kahlo 's achievement a a specifically mexican painter , operating within the particularity of her historical moment .
more problematic is the way in which such a dislocation ha led to the acceptance of her â€˜ mexicanness â€™ a mere decoration of the essentially feminist theme of her work , thereby defusing a substantial part of the art described by breton a a â€˜ ribbon round a bomb â€™ .
it is the ribbon that run through the page of vogue , the glossy surface of the image in direct opposition to a work such a kahlo 's the suicide of dorothy hale ( 1939 ) ( fig. 9 ) .
in this painting , a memorial to a woman 's tragic death is transformed into an indictment of the culture which destroyed her .
hale 's suicide became a poignant metaphor for the oppressive nature of the social value of new york and north america in general .
the story behind hale 's death wa one with which kahlo obviously identified , and within which dress formed an important symbolic function .
before jumping from the window of her apartment , hale had dressed meticulously in her most flattering dress , the corsage of yellow rose a gift from a male admirer .
in kahlo 's painting , the figure fall from the fantasy world she ha inhabited to the harsh bloodspattered reality of the street , literally coming down to earth .
hale 's eye stare knowingly at the viewer , a human sacrifice to an alienated and consumerist culture .
the horizontality of her fallen body is juxtaposed to the vertical thrust of the apartment building .
she leap from an architectural monument to a phallocentric world .
although destroyed , she ha also escaped .
the painting , dedicated to hale 's mother , wa commissioned by a mutual friend of kahlo and dorothy hale , the managing editor of vanity fair , clare boothe luce .
the painting wa agreed to by luce in part to recompense for what she saw a her misjudgment of her dead friend .
having lent hale money to pay her rent she had been angered to discover her spending enormous sum on an haute-couture dress , and refused to turn up to what , in retrospect , became hale 's farewell party .
later it wa revealed that the money had come from a different source .
a male friend had tried to dissuade hale from seeking a much needed job and had given her a thousand dollar to buy â€˜ the most beautiful dress in new york â€™ , telling her that what she needed wa to find a rich husband .
on one level this work deal with a generalised â€˜ woman 's experience â€™ , yet the metaphorical power of dorothy hale 's dress derives from kahlo 's use of clothing in her own self-portrait .
dress not only cover and decorates the body but instils in the wearer it own characteristic strength and weakness .
hale 's black velvet dress is cursed because it represents the value of the â€˜ gringolandia â€™ so hated by kahlo .
in those painting where kahlo wear european dress she is passive , weak and unable to control her own destiny , but in the tehuana costume she is strong , powerful , hopeful .
unclothed , her body becomes yet more vulnerable , but a jean franco state :
the unclothed body is not a â€˜ self but a socialised body , a body that is opened by instrument , technologized , wounded , it organ displayed to the outside world .
the â€˜ inner â€™ frida is controlled by modern society far more than the clothed frida , who often mark her deviation from the norm by defiantly returning the gaze of the viewer .
kahlo 's naked body becomes not just the tortured self of her personal biography but a visual counterpart to the injured and defiled manifestation of mexico 's colonised past : la llorona â€˜ the weeping woman â€™ of popular myth and la chingada , the raped and abused mother described in paz 's the labyrinth of solitude .
descended from an aztec mother goddess , llorona is a long-suffering mother figure , symbolic in a wider sense of the trauma of the spanish invasion .
driven mad with grief by the loss of her child , she is thought to wander the street weeping and cry out a ghostly memory of the pre-conquest past .
at it most simple , la chingada , a the mother of mestizo culture is â€˜ the mother forcibly opened , violated or deceived â€™ .
the female soil possessed and misused by the masculine force of the spanish invader .
the indian mexico raped and abused by the conquistador yet bearing his bastard child .
the rhetoric of the tehuana opposes the nihilism of traditional feminisation of colonial trauma , and asserts the potential of a dignified cultural resistance .

a major , though often ignored , work by kahlo demonstrates the cultural politics underlying her art .
my dress hang there ( 1939 ) ( fig. 10 ) is one of the artist â€™ s most formally adventurous work , mixing photographic collage with paint to produce a critique of north american culture .
kahlo doe not appear in the work , her tehuana costume hang empty in the centre of the composition , suspended between a toilet bowl and a golfing trophy .
on one level my dress â€¦ is a coda to self-portrait on the borderline ( 1932 ) ( fig. 11 ) of the previous year .
this small painting on metal , in the style of a catholic votive image , show the artist poised between the technological inhumanity of a capitalist north america and the archaic fertility of mexico .
interwoven with these image are subtler reference to the metaphorical borderline which separate latin american culture from that of europe and north america .
this is done by a series of juxtaposition ; the past versus the present ; female nature versus masculine technology ; growth versus exploitation ; and in it very material presence , the tradition of fine art versus the popular .
at the same time the ambivalence of her own , and modern mexico 's position is manifested in the figure of the artist .
the paper flag of her homeland is contrasted to the modernity of the cigarette held in her other hand .
the red and green of the aztec necklace link it compositionally with the indigenous plant to the â€˜ south â€™ of the painting , the pink colonial-style dress tonally blending with the skyscraper to the â€˜ north â€™ .
my dress â€¦ again suggests a conflict , but the ambivalence is gone .
nature ha been banished , technology and it concomitant value reign over a harshly masculine world .
three element refer to the female presence , all of them dealing with an essential lack .
the empty dress , a peeling poster of mae west and in the far distance the statue of liberty .
fig. 10 .
frida kahlo : my dress hang there , 1933 , 46x50 cm , estate of dr .
leo eloesser .
although occasionally humorous , the work present a bleak view of urban alienation .
the church , wall street , and industry are joined by a network of telephone line , forming a remorsely inhuman environment .
beneath this man-made mechanism of oppression are the people , literally distanced from their surroundings by kahlo 's use of photo-collage .
in the forefront of this scene flutter the dress , incongruously vibrant despite it suggestion of loss .
dislocated from it political context , it hang like a piã±ata above the teeming street of the city ; decorative yet potentially explosive .
there is no place â€˜ there â€™ for the value the tehuana dress represents , it fold are given meaning by kahlo 's search for a cultural identity .
within the confines of the painting it becomes a silent emblem of protest , a reminder of political alternative .
the physicality so characteristic of kahlo 's work is missing , no flesh , no blood , just the tawdriness of the peeling poster and the hollow reminder of lost liberty .
the inter-relationship of body and dress so self-consciously referred to in many of kahlo 's most polemical work ( fig. 12 ) ha been strangely inverted by her current popularity .
her â€˜ mexicanness â€™ ha become a stylistic gloss , decorative , colourful , pretty , even individualistic .
the colonised body which kahlo clothed in revolutionary idealism ha lost it function a a symbol of nationhood becoming instead an icon of female suffering .
what is obscured by this process is that it wa through clothing , in both art and life , that kahlo attempted to redress the wrong of history .

parliament urged to think again on housing issue : .
queen 's bench divisional court sandwell metropolitan borough council v bujok before lord justice watkins and mr justice hutchison november 2 1989
if a dwelling house is in such a state of disrepair a to be prejudicial to health or a nuisance , the tenant may lay an information against his landlord alleging the existence of a statutory nuisance under the public health act 1936 .
the tenant is not obliged to ensure that the landlord is aware of the defect in the premise or to give the landlord an opportunity to remedy the defect before commencing legal proceeding .
although that is the position in law , the court emphasised that a a matter of commonm_sense a tenant should first complain to the landlord before exercising the right to prosecute .
the fact .
mr bujok and her family occupied a house a council tenant .
in september 1988 mr bujok laid an information against the council alleging the existence and continuance of a statutory nuisance under section 92(1) of the public health act 1936 .
it wa alleged that the council , being the owner of the premise , were the person by whose act , default or sufferance the nuisance arose .
prior to laying the information mr bujok had not served an abatement notice upon the council or informed them of the alleged defect in the premise .
the justice held mr bujok wa not required to ensure that the council were aware of the defective state of the property prior to laying the information .
the council appealed by case stated .
the legislation .
section 92(1) of the 1936 act defines â€˜ statutory nuisance â€™ a â€˜ any premise in such a state a to be prejudicial to health or a nuisance â€™ .
the decision .
mr justice hutchison said the 1936 act primarily envisages a system where the local authority ha a power and a duty to try to secure that premise are not in a state which constitutes a statutory nuisance .
action is initiated by the service of an abatement notice requiring remedial work .
if the person in default fails to comply with an abatement notice the local authority is obliged to make a complaint to the magistrate .
if the complaint is proved , a nuisance order is made requiring the defendant to get the necessary work done .
effectively the sequence is that the person in default is told what is wrong and is required to put it right .
he is given an opportunity to do so , and if he doe not , he is subject to sanction by the court to compel him to do so .
the problem arises in connection with section 99 which adapts or applies the provision to case where an individual rather than the local authority wish to make the complaint .
need he serve an abatement notice ?
the authority plainly establish that he need not and can not do so .
doe that mean he may lay an information and bring the matter before the magistrate without first putting the person alleged to be in default on notice of what is alleged ?
the council argued that a landlord , particularly one such a a local authority , can not realistically be expected to have a system of inspection of all it premise and in practice is entitled to depend upon notification by it tenant .
for mr bujok it wa argued that the 1936 act wa designed to secure in the interest of the community at large that statutory nuisance did not exist .
it wa submitted that an owner can not turn his back on his property because when he purchase and take on the responsibility of letting , he know the property will in the course of time deteriorate .
he must therefore satisfy himself on a regular basis that it doe not constitute a statutory nuisance .
in warner v lambeth london borough council ( 1985 ) 15 hlr 45 , 50 , lord justice glidewell said a private person could lay an information alleging the failure to abate a statutory nuisance without first giving notice requiring abatement .
therefore in the present case the justice came to the correct conclusion .
his lordship reached that decision without enthusiasm because it seemed that a a matter of common sense , notice should be given in such circumstance before criminal proceeding were launched .
lord justice watkins said he agreed with reluctance .
it wa surely repugnant to commonm_sense that in this area of legal activity a local authority should be prosecuted by one of it tenant without first being given the opportunity by that tenant to remedy the consequence of a neglect to repair the dwelling that the tenant occupied .
in law there wa no doubt that mr bujok wa entitled to commence proceeding without giving notice of the state of the dwelling to the council .
but in every other conceivable way that action wa entirely wrong .
endless trouble to many people in court and council office and much money could be saved by the giving of notice of disrepair .
if the council did not react to that notice , then would be the time for the tenant to exercise the right to prosecute .
parliament should give fresh thought to enacting a provision placing an obligation upon a council tenant to give notice to the council before being permitted to commence proceeding .
appearance : john cherryman qc instructed by sherwood & co for the council ; elizabeth norman instructed by michael arnold & co , oldbury , for mr bujok .
shiranikha herbert barrister
leinster face an uphill task .
by robert armstrong in dublin
the all black begin the irish leg of their 13-match tour at lansdowne road today against leinster , who have never beaten a major touring side .
leinster have named a team that look strong on paper , including eight international , yet they recently lost to both munster and ulster in the inter-provincial championship .
such is the mood of pessimism here it is hard to find anyone who belief the all black , having won their seven match in wale , will face any significant threat during the next fortnight .
ulster , the provincial champion , may well fancy their chance on november 21 , but leinster look certain to face an uphill struggle even though the tourist have rested 13 of the team that beat wale .
leinster will be hard pushed to keep the score within the respectable margin of defeat set by their predecessor .
in 1964 the all black defeated leinster 11-5 , they won 17-8 in 1972 and scraped home 8-3 in 1974 .
however , during the eighty irish provincial rugby ha assumed a third world status in relation to new zealand 's .
leinster have been undermined by their failure to secure prestige fixture since the mid-seventies .
when new zealand last toured ireland in 1978 leinster were ignored .
the same thing happened in 1984 when the province wa denied a fixture against the wallaby .
such neglect ha done nothing for their confidence .
even so , the all black , who include seven capped player , will give today 's opponent due respect .
a their coach , alex wyllie , remarked : â€˜ when we arrived in wale we were told cardiff were no damned good and look how well they played against u .

the tourist will field four back aged 21 or under .
for their part , leinster are boosted by the presence of four player already selected for ireland to play new zealand in dublin on november 18 .
they are brendan mullin , the lion centre , fergus aherne , the scrum-half , and the two new cap , nick popplewell at loose-head and brian smith , the fly-half .
no doubt smith , the oxford university australian , who won five cap for the wallaby , will feel a bit closer to home facing the all black twice in the next 11 day .
it will be fascinating to see how smith , a gifted all-round footballer , shape up in his prospective international partnership with aherne .
equally intriguing will be the line-out performance of the young london irish lock , neil francis , who ha been left out of the current ireland squad .

by stephen bierley
oldham athletic , who had never beaten a first division side since they dropped into the second division in 1923 , made up for 66 year of not altogether patient waiting with a pulsating victory over the league champion arsenal at boundary park last night .
the pennines fairly shook .
no supporter of the latics dared dream it , but suddenly the improbable wa a throbbing , joyous reality .
two goal from the irrepressible andy ritchie , his 13th and 14th this season , and a third by the 20-year-old midfield player nick henry , and arsenal were sunk with only the trace of a last-minute goal by quinn .
despite many and varied flurry of activity in the first 40 minute , arsenal seemed reasonably secure if not inspired .
they held their line and competed hard in midfield , damping down oldham 's initial verve and preparing themselves for more of the same in the second half .
then oldham struck .
winterburn almost put the ball into his own net from milligan 's cross , o'leary recovering an awkward situation .
almost immediately smith had an excellent chance for arsenal but stumbled .
oldham took up the attack again and barlow , who had a fine match at left-back , totally containing rocastle , floated in a deep cross beyond winterburn .

arsenal had no choice but to attack a soon a the second half began .

from the resulting corner rhodes made another fine save , hurtling to his right to deflect away dixon 's rising shot .
finally , with arsenal pressing hard , he clawed away quinn 's careful header from thomas 's drag-back .
quinn held his head in disbelief .
worse , far worse wa to follow .
bunn , who scored six goal in the previous round against scarborough , this time turned into the provider , putting milligan clear and free .
he wa hauled back on the edge of the area by o'leary , a â€˜ professional â€™ foul for which the arsenal central defender wa booked .
holden 's 64th-minute free-kick clattered the wall and the ball fell to henry , who drilled a low shot from more than 30 yard inside lukic 's right-hand post .
in another 10 minute any remaining oldham doubt were dispelled .
ritchie passed to irwin and then ran on to head the cross past lukic .
arsenal were stitched and stuffed , with no question of a fluke .
not for the first time this season their defence had been found wanting and oldham exploited the weakness to the full , owing a special debt to the inspiration and tireless running of henry and milligan .
george graham wa not amused .
he called his team 's performance â€˜ unacceptable â€™ .
but he also said : â€˜ let's not take any credit away from oldham .
they were tremendous , and outplayed u in the first half .
the plastic pitch is no excuse .
we trained on an artificial pitch for two day this week and we should have done a lot better . â€™
joe royle , the oldham manager , wa full of praise both for graham and his own team .
â€˜ george wa brilliant , â€™ he said .
â€˜ he could have blamed this and that but he said we deserved it .
the manager 's attitude show why they are champion .
he took it on the chin .
â€˜ one or two people will be ready to put this down to plastic but our goal were nothing to do with plastic .

prototyping is crucial to system development , argues ian richards tailored to fit .
in system development nothing is more fundamental than assessing user requirement .
if you do n't know what the system is required to do ; you do n't know anything .
but many system developer are unable to ass requirement properly .
they seem to think that you can ask a businessman what his requirement are and get an answer that amount to a draft system specification .
a doctor doe n't ask his patient what treatment to prescribe .
the patient can explain only what the problem is .
it is the doctor that provides the remedy .
if you ask a user what sort of system he want you will be met with a blank look .
a user may have a deep knowledge of business problem , but knowing little about computer , ha no idea how they should be tackled .
yet , analyst are heard asking time and again , â€˜ tell me what you want .
we 've gone awaym_from the day of system imposed by the data processing department , this is going to be a system for the user . â€™
but of course the user do n't know what they want , so they end up getting another duff system .
an effective analyst provides the same service to the business a the doctor provides to the patient .
he find out what the need of the business are , and prescribes the cure .
the user tell the analyst what the problem are , and the analyst decides , at least in broad term , what the user requires .
but the analyst ha one great advantage over the doctor .
once the user becomes familiar with the proposed system , helpful comment come thick and fast .
â€˜ oh , this will be of great help in ordering raw material , but sometimes we get part delivery , could we have an extra facility to deal with those ?
and sometimes non-standard discount is given , a pig to deal with on the old system , but if you could add one extra input box on that screen there â€¦
and what about order not delivered on time ?
if we could list those we 'd have advance warning of shortage problem on the assembly line two month before they occur .
now that would be a great leap forward . â€™
unfortunately you can not reach this stage until you have developed a prototype system .
and you ca n't develop a prototype system because the user have n't got a clue what they want .
most of them are probably muttering , â€˜ i 'm too busy to get involved in this sort of thing .
what 's wrong with the old system anyway ? â€™
the only way to develop a prototype is for the analyst to get inside the head of the user and , thinking like a user , decide what sort of system is required .
of course , the initial system will not be perfect .
the analyst can not hope to understand the business a well in a few week a the user doe after many year .
but once the user see the system , channel of communication will open .
instead of persuading the user to specify requirement , the analyst will be driven by the user to meet key need .
good system development go through two distinct phase .
initially the analyst doe all the work , leading the user towards a system he think is right for the business .
but once the user see the potential of the system , a change in attitude take place .
the process becomes demand driven by the user .
the analyst is then forced on the defensive , explaining why new feature can not be included because they are technically difficult or prohibitively expensive .
traditionally , system were validated by user agreeing functional specification .
in theory , validation meant that the user had read the specification , imagined how the system would work in practice , and agreed the design .
it wa only when using a â€˜ test â€™ version of the system ( available just before the planned implementation date ) that difficulty would come to light , and a host of change request be issued .
the advent of fourth generation language ( 4gls ) ha made system development much easier .
with a 4gl an initial prototype can be put together quickly .
this mean feedback is obtained early in the development process , and the system can grow around the user 's requirement .
crucial to the development process is the relationship built up between the analyst and the user .
the best system arise when both have a deep understanding of each other 's job .
many developer use business analyst to ensure that the development team maintain a proper focus on business requirement .
but this can be counter-productive , a it cut off communication between the system analyst and the user .
too much specialisation is bad for system development ; it feed the temptation to get engrossed in technical difficulty and forget about the underlying business need .
if you should stroll into a pub and meet an analyst and a user talking about work , and you can not tell one from the other , they have probably developed a successful system together .
ian richards ' book , how to use a computer to improve your business , ha just been published by graham & trotman ( â£8.95 paperback ; â£16 hardback ) .
tel : 01-821 1123 .

edoardo amaldi .
ragazzi of distinction : .
in december , 1943 , the men working feverishly to create the first american atomic bomb sent a team of â€˜ spook â€™ to naples .
one of their main assignment wa to contact edoardo amaldi , a physicist thought to be in hiding near rome .
six month later , the day before rome 's liberation by the ally , amaldi wa found .
he wa interviewed by moe berg , then one of the most famous baseball player in america .
berg wa also an agent of the office of strategic service , which wa later to give birth to the cia .
his job wa to convince amaldi to pack his bag because there wa a ship waiting at naples to take him to the united state .
amaldi 's presence there had been sought by two other italian colleague , also physicist .
his mentor , enrico fermi , later to be called â€˜ the father of the bomb â€™ , and emilio segre ( who died in california earlier this year ) .
amaldi dodged the american invitation , perhaps because ( with rome liberated ) fermi 's mantle in physic had fallen on his young shoulder and there were younger mind to teach .
he wore that mantle well at rome university until his retirement in 1978 .
but amaldi never really retired nor grew old .
he kept regular hour in the university 's physic building , spoke at scientific meeting this year in moscow and washington .
a president of the accademia nazionale dei lincei he had delivered the welcoming address on tuesday to a symposium of scientist .
he then ordered a car to call for him the next morning for a similar occasion and wa felled by a stroke while waiting for the lift .
amaldi grew up in a small town in lombardy , and took his doctorate in physic from rome at the remarkably early age of 21 .
in 1929 , he became one of the ragazzi di via panisperna â€” the street where fermi 's â€˜ kid â€™ carried out their own experiment under the master in their own under-financed lab .
emilio segre wa one kid , and bruno pontecorvo , later to defect from britain to the soviet union , another .
it is interesting to note that the â€˜ pope â€™ â€” a the kid called fermi â€” â€˜ because he 's always right â€™ , wa only seven year older than amaldi .
amaldi astounded his group in october 1934 with his discovery that by slowing down , rather than accelerating , neutron , he could provoke intense nuclear reaction .
he held a chair in physic from 1937 until his retirement publishing more than 150 paper on atomic and nuclear physic .
he wa awarded honorary degree by algiers , glasgow and oxford .
he became a founder , and active executive , of the european centre for nuclear research in geneva .
i had the pleasure of two long talk last year with professor amaldi about his knowledge of what the german physicist were doing with their atom during the war year .
apart for his incongruously white hair , amaldi seemed to have the mental lucidity and expected energy of a man half his age .
his modesty , considering his world-wide fame in his field , wa endearing .
i knew almost nothing about physic but we shared some joke about the rome telephone system .
in 1949 , amaldi wrote to the italian prime minister asking for permission to produce and sell sealing wax for letter , â€˜ so that we may raise needed fund for our physic lab â€™ .
the reply came from an under-secretary who said that the present funding wa considered adequate and the commercial undertaking would be ill-advised .
it wa signed by giulio andreotti , the present prime minister .
george armstrong edoardo amaldi , born carpaneto piacentino september 5 , 1908 ; died rome , december 5 , 1989 .
midwife at the birth of a state .
the intifada is a people 's unarmed revolution against occupation .
it two main slogan , repeated countless time in the directive issued by the underground leadership , are freedom and independence .
it ha employed a dual strategy to achieve these two objective .
first , a comprehensive civil disobedience campaign wa begun by which people severed , or minimised , all the contact point by which they were bound to the israeli occupation authority .
this campaign included resignation of palestinian official from public post , the boycott of israeli good and product , and the refusal to pay tax and fine .
partial and full strike , demonstration , sit-in , convention â€¦ all these have in fact only constituted the outer layer of an inner mechanism of civilian rebellion .
the second , and complementary , part of the intifada strategy concentrated on the construction of an indigenous national authority .
a israel 's authority wa being lifted , the population began creating an alternative authority of their own .
popular committee were established in village , refugee camp , suburb , street , in fact in every community .
some headway wa made in expanding self-sufficiency , whether through utilising more land for agriculture , developing home economy , or encouraging local manufacturer and product .
village and refugee camp were thus being developed into â€˜ liberated â€™ or â€˜ independent â€™ area , if not militarily , then at least psychologically , politically and infrastructurally .
bloody clash would occur whenever armoured unit raided these village , storming through makeshift defensive road block and responding to rock being thrown with live bullet and tear gas ; but no sooner would these army unit be gone than authority would revert to the village resident .
palestinian flag would be raised on minaret and church spire , road block would again be erected , and life in all it aspect would once again be run by the local leadership .
the structure of the developing national authority ha been both diffuse enough to prevent it from being destroyed by any one single sweep of arrest ( there have been more than 50,000 arrest since the intifada 's outbreak ) , and coherent enough to allow for the existence of a unified resistance strategy .
while the entire network of popular committee , local institution and the general public constitute the field commander in the battle of civilian disobedience and of constructing a political infrastructure , a rotating unified national command act in the role of field-general , issuing a bi-monthly directive outlining policy and determining specific resistance programme .
a high level of mobility in the structure allows for continuous interchange of role and idea , and retains for the unified national command the closeness to grass root that is required to make it truly reflect people 's wish and sentiment .
this expanded network of popular committee and institution making up the unified leadership is infused by ten of thousand of activist who belong to , or identify with , the different faction of the plo .
in effect , therefore , the plo exists at all level of organisation within the occupied territory .
thus the palestinian national movement both inside and outside the occupied territory is an organic whole .
the pattern of the intifada ha been cyclical .
thrust of resistance ( mass demonstration , resignation , tax rebellion , etc ) would come in crest .
the pattern is determined by a wide variety of factor , including what the israeli army doe .
but the relation is complex , not uni-directional .
harsh measure â€” putting an entire community under an absolute curfew for a continuous lengthy period of time , demolishing home , uprooting olive or citrus tree , physical intimidation and terror tactic employed by raiding army unit , shooting , killing , cutting off water or electricity supply and telephone link to village or town , mass arrest , intimidatory interrogation technique â€” can either create a temporary lull or activate an eruption .
the army never know which it will be .
it is a if it is walking through a minefield .
the wave-like pattern of the intifada , it pain and suffering , are all reminiscent of the process of birth .
the metaphor is apt , a palestinian regard themselves a engaging in a process of giving birth to their independent palestinian state .
through their revolution , the mass are both mother and midwife to the birth of this state .
the intifada is the midwife of freedom .
through it , palestinian are struggling on a daily basis to shake off israel 's authority and to construct their own .
the struggle reflects a revolution in mass consciousness , by which people have come to realise that idea and aspiration must be embodied in manifest act if reality is to be changed .
thus , wherever one look , one find people engaged in the construction of the block that will make up the palestinian state .
it is a conscious effort .
the mass are being engaged in the craft of state-masonry .
in this process of state building , many stage have been covered .
the declaration of independence issued by the palestine national council ( pnc ) on november 15 last year constitutes a major landmark along this road .
it significance lie in it double message : that the aim of the palestinian struggle is the establishment of palestinian independence , and that this independence is regarded a being not at israel 's expense .
this ha been a constant theme of intifada policy : that we wish to build ( palestine ) , not to destroy ( israel ) ; that we wish to achieve freedom ( for our people ) , not to deprive others ( israeli ) of it ; that we wish to protect and save life ( ours ) , not to endanger the life of others ( israeli ) .
in one of several intifada leaflet written in hebrew and addressed to the israeli soldier on duty in the occupied territory , the message wa repeated : soldier , go home .
return to your family and child .
be with them in peace so that we may remain with our family and child in peace .
we do not wish to harm you , or your state .
we wish to be unharmed , in our own state .
how can the process of state building be developed ?
if the pnc declaration of independence constituted a major landmark in this process , the time ha come to embark on another major step , that of declaring the setting up of a state or government structure .
an escalation of the intifada in this direction would serve two purpose at once .
first , it would consolidate the structure of the developing national authority which is competing to replace the occupation authority .
second , it would consolidate the image and essence of the intifada a a constructive , not a destructive , force .
naturally , to embark on such a step is not necessarily to succeed immediately in realising it .
rather , it is a challenge .
it will be a further challenge to israel 's occupation , conceived in the image of earlier challenge of the intifada .
but it will also be a challenge to u , palestinian , summoning u to work more energetically towards the idea 's fulfilment .
it would be a natural extension of the intifada 's dual strategy towards disengagement from israel , and the corresponding process of state building .
it would further naturalise and legitimise the evolving skeletal form of palestinian independence .
it would provide the multitudinous popular committee and activity with a more advanced form of organisation and structure .
it would enable better planning and performance .
it would maximise civilian tactic of resistance and defuse the natural potential for violence , containing and eventually eliminating the marginal but intrusive phenomenon of collaborator activation by israeli security authority and collaborator execution by local palestinian .
it would create a further fact that would put israel on the spot .
israel 's reaction , however hostile , could only further our cause .
arresting or deporting the ten of thousand of palestinian professional who would be employed in perfectly apolitical , harmless and humanitarian job can only further isolate the israeli government .
half-way measure can only imply half-way success .
a modus vivendi would also imply success .
in general , our policy should be to proceed with building our state block by block , without waiting to be given a gift of it through negotiation .
we should regard negotiation rather a the mean by which we could establish formal agreement between our state and israel .
such agreement can range from the issue of border to the issue of free wave-lengths for our future television and radio network .
in the meantime , we have the capacity to bring coherence and organisation to a whole range of activity , further consolidating the institutional linkage between the people in the occupied state and the plo leadership .
entire department can be set up , in health , foreign affair , agriculture , trade , finance , education , justice , religion , information and social welfare .
a pyramid administrative structure , establishing link from popular committee in village right up to the executive committee of the plo ( in it capacity a a cabinet ) , can be established .
during the intifada the people have been engaged in building the side wall .
a government would provide the roof which would bring these wall together .
it would add another necessary touch in the process of creating a palestinian home .
sari nusseibeh , a leading palestinian intellectual , is professor of philosophy at bir zeit , the west bank university closed by the israeli early last year .
his idea are widely influential among palestinian .
nusseibeh â€¦
