friday 16 september to tuesday 20 september
once free of the knotted tentacle of the eastern suburb , dalgliesh made good time and by three he wa driving through lydsett village .
here a right turn took him off the coastal road on to what wa little more than a smoothly macadamed track bordered by water-filled ditch and fringed by a golden haze of reed , their lumbered head straining in the wind .
and now , for the first time , he thought that he could smell the north sea , that potent but half-illusory tang evoking nostalgic memory of childhood holiday , of solitary adolescent walk a he struggled with his first poem , of his aunt 's tall figure at his side , binoculars round her neck , striding towards the haunt of her beloved bird .
and here , barring the road , wa the familiar old farm gate still in place .
it continued presence always surprised him since it served no purpose that he could see except symbolically to cut off the headland and to give traveller pause to consider whether they really wanted to continue .
it swung open at his touch but closing it , a always , wa more difficult and he lugged and half lifted it into place and slipped the circle of wire over the gatepost with a familiar sensation of having turned his back on the workaday world and entered country which , no matter how frequent his visit , would always be alien territory .
he wa driving now across the open headland towards the fringe of pine tree which bordered the north sea .
the only house to his left wa the old victorian rectory , a square , red-brick building , incongruous behind it struggling hedge of rhododendron and laurel .
to his right the ground rose gently towards the southern cliff and he could see the dark mouth of a concrete pillbox , undemolished since the war , and a seemingly indestructible a the great hulk of wave-battered concrete , remnant of the old fortification which lay half-submerged in the sand along part of the beach .
to the north the broken arch and stump of the ruined benedictine abbey gleamed golden in the afternoon sun against the crinkled blue of the sea and , breasting a small ridge , he glimpsed for the first time the topsail of larksoken mill and beyond it , against the skyline , the great grey bulk of larksoken nuclear power station .
the road he wa on , veering left , would lead eventually to the station but wa , he knew , seldom used since normal traffic and all heavy vehicle used the new access road to the north .
the headland wa empty and almost bare , the few straggling tree , distorted by the wind , struggled to keep their precarious hold in the uncompromising soil .
and now he wa passing a second and more dilapidated pillbox and it struck him that the whole headland had the desolate look of an old battlefield , the corps long since carted away but the air vibrating still with the gunfire of long-lost battle , while the power station loomed over it like a grandiose modern monument to the unknown dead .
on his previous visit to larksoken he had seen martyr 's cottage spread out beneath him when he and his aunt had stood surveying the headland from the small top room under the cone of the mill .
but he had never been closer to it than the road and now , driving up to it , it struck him again that the description â€˜ cottage â€™ wa hardly appropriate .

the conversation wa exclusively on the subject of the discovery at wyvis hall .
adam did not know whether to be glad or sorry he had not obtained an english newspaper while away .
if he had done the shock would have been le but on the other hand , his holiday would have been spoilt .
he would have liked very much to be alone .
of course he knew there wa no possibility of this , now or when he returned home , for when you were married you never could be alone .
presumably that wa the point .
what wa he going to tell anne ?
how much wa he going to tell her ?
he did n't know .
none of it , if he could help it .

â€˜ he had a beard then , anne . â€™

they had to wait until his father wa ready .

it wa possible they might be waiting for him .
they would wish to interview every former owner or occupant of wyvis hall .
he looked again at the newspaper account of the adjourned inquest that his father had saved for him .
